This seems backwards - if wholeWord is true, shouldn't we be checking for `\\b` (actual word boundaries) rather than their negation? I see the issue now. The regex `\\\\B` in the test is actually looking for a literal backslash followed by 'B', not testing for a word boundary assertion. The logic seems confused about what it's trying to check.\n\nThe intent should be to add `\\b` word boundaries if they're not already present at the start and end of the pattern. So I'd need to check if the pattern already begins with `\\b` using something like `/^\\\\b/.test(searchString)`, and if it doesn't, prepend the boundary. The current approach of testing a single character against `\\B` doesn't accomplish this.\n\nThis looks like a bug where `\\B` (non-word boundary) got used instead of `\\b` (word boundary).
